This is here mainly for convenient internal use such\\n41: // as in test cases.\\n42: func (po *PlanOpts) ApplyOpts() *ApplyOpts {\\n43: \\treturn &ApplyOpts{\\n44: \\t\\tExternalProviders: po.ExternalProviders,\\n45: \\t}\\n46: }\\n47: \\n48: // Apply performs the actions described by the given Plan object and returns\\n49: // the resulting updated state.\\n50: //\\n51: // The given configuration *must* be the same configuration that was passed\\n52: // earlier to Context.Plan in order to create this plan.\\n53: //\\n54: // Even if the returned diagnostics contains errors, Apply always returns the\\n55: // resulting state which is likely to have been partially-updated.\\n56: //\\n57: // The [opts] argument may be nil to indicate that no special options are\\n58: // required. In that case, Apply will use a default set of options. Some\\n59: // options in [PlanOpts] when creating a plan must be echoed with equivalent\\n60: // settings during apply, so leaving opts as nil might not be valid for\\n61: // certain combinations of plan-time options.\\n62: func (c *Context) Apply(plan *plans.Plan, config *configs.Config, opts *ApplyOpts) (*states.State, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\\n63: \\tstate, _, diags := c.ApplyAndEval(plan, config, opts)\\n64: \\treturn state, diags\\n65: }\\n66: \\n67: // ApplyAndEval is like [Context.Apply] except that it additionally makes a\\n68: // best effort to return a [lang.Scope] which can evaluate expressions in the\\n69: // root module based on the content of the new state.\\n70: //\\n71: // The scope will be nil if the apply process doesn't complete successfully\\n72: // enough to produce a valid evaluation scope. If the returned state is nil\\n73: // then the scope will always be nil, but it's also possible for the scope\\n74: // to be nil even when the state isn't, if the apply didn't complete enough for\\n75: // the evaluation scope to produce consistent results.\\n76: func (c *Context) ApplyAndEval(plan *plans.Plan, config *configs.Config, opts *ApplyOpts) (*states.State, *lang.Scope, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\\n77: \\tdefer c.acquireRun(\\\"apply\\\")()\\n78: \\tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\\n79: \\n80: \\tif plan == nil {\\n81: \\t\\tpanic(\\\"cannot apply nil plan\\\")\\n82: \\t}\\n83: \\tlog.Printf(\\\"[DEBUG] Building and walking apply graph for %s plan\\\", plan.UIMode)\\n84: \\n85: \\tif opts == nil {\\n86: \\t\\topts = &ApplyOpts{}\\n87: \\t}\\n88: \\n89: \\tif plan.Errored {\\n90: \\t\\tdiags = diags.Append(tfdiags.Sourceless(\\n91: \\t\\t\\ttfdiags.Error,\\n92: \\t\\t\\t\\\"Cannot apply failed plan\\\",\\n93: \\t\\t\\t`The given plan is incomplete due to errors during planning, and so it cannot be applied.`,\\n94: \\t\\t))\\n95: \\t\\treturn nil, nil, diags\\n96: \\t}\\n97: \\tif !plan.Applyable {\\n98: \\t\\tif plan.Changes.Empty() {\\n99: \\t\\t\\t// If a plan is not applyable but it didn't have any errors then that\\n100: \\t\\t\\t// suggests it was a \\\"no-op\\\" plan, which doesn't really do any\\n101: \\t\\t\\t// harm to apply, so we'll just do it but leave ourselves a note\\n102: \\t\\t\\t// in the trace log in case it ends up relevant to a bug report.\\n103: \\t\\t\\tlog.Printf(\\\"[TRACE] Applying a no-op plan\\\")\\n104: \\t\\t} else {\\n105: \\t\\t\\t// This situation isn't something we expect, since our own rules\\n106: \\t\\t\\t// for what \\\"applyable\\\" means make this scenario impossible. We'll\\n107: \\t\\t\\t// reject it on the assumption that something very strange is\\n108: \\t\\t\\t// going on. and so better to halt than do something incorrect.\\n109: \\t\\t\\t// This error message is generic and useless because we don't\\n110: \\t\\t\\t// expect anyone to ever see it in normal use.\\n111: \\t\\t\\tdiags = diags.Append(tfdiags.Sourceless(\\n112: \\t\\t\\t\\ttfdiags.Error,\\n113: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\\"Cannot apply non-applyable plan\\\",\\n114: \\t\\t\\t\\t`The given plan is not applyable. {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01Tooj84Ln9g9kP4ijKHcc8R","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_017zkkenT1M4TxFRzvDVYNVJ","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/workspace/documentation.md","content":"# Terraform Plan/Apply Pipeline Architecture Documentation\n\n## Overview\n\nTerraform's plan/apply pipeline is built on a graph-based execution model where infrastructure operations are represented as directed acyclic graphs (DAGs). The architecture enables concurrent execution of independent operations while maintaining correct ordering of dependent operations.\n\nThe pipeline consists of three major phases:\n1. **Graph Construction** - Building a DAG of operations from configuration\n2. **Graph Traversal** - Executing graph nodes in dependency order\n3. **State Management** - Tracking and persisting infrastructure state\n\n## 1. Graph Builder System\n\n### 1.1 GraphBuilder Interface\n\nThe `GraphBuilder` interface is the foundational abstraction for constructing execution graphs:\n\n```go\ntype GraphBuilder interface {\n    Build(addrs.ModuleInstance) (*Graph, tfdiags.Diagnostics)\n}\n```\n\nGraph builders take configuration, state, and options as input and produce a complete execution graph ready for traversal.\n\n### 1.2 BasicGraphBuilder\n\nThe `BasicGraphBuilder` is the core implementation that applies a sequence of transformations:\n\n```go\ntype BasicGraphBuilder struct {\n    Steps []GraphTransformer\n    Name  string\n}\n\nfunc (b *BasicGraphBuilder) Build(path addrs.ModuleInstance) (*Graph, tfdiags.Diagnostics)\n```\n\nThe Build method:\n1. Creates an empty graph at the given module path\n2. Sequentially applies each GraphTransformer\n3. Validates the final graph structure\n4. Returns diagnostics for any errors during transformation\n\nEach transformer can add nodes, modify edges, or reorganize the graph structure. Transformers are applied in a specific order to ensure correct graph construction.\n\n### 1.3 Operation-Specific Graph Builders\n\n#### PlanGraphBuilder\n\nBuilds graphs for plan and plan-like operations (plan, plan-destroy, validate, import):\n\n**Key inputs:**\n- `Config` - The desired infrastructure configuration\n- `State` - The current state (for comparison)\n- `RootVariableValues` - Input variables for the root module\n- `ExternalProviderConfigs` - Pre-configured provider instances\n- `Targets` - Resource targeting for partial operations\n- `ForceReplace` - Resources to force replacement\n- `skipRefresh` - Whether to skip state refresh\n- `skipPlanChanges` - For refresh-only operations\n\n**Graph composition:**\n1. Creates resource nodes from configuration\n2. Attaches provider configurations and schemas\n3. Establishes dependencies based on references\n4. Handles count/for_each expansion\n5. Attaches validation and check nodes\n6. Applies targeting filters if specified\n\n#### ApplyGraphBuilder\n\nBuilds graphs for applying previously-generated plans:\n\n**Key inputs:**\n- `Config` - The configuration file (must match the plan's configuration)\n- `Changes` - The planned changes from the plan file\n- `State` - Current state used as a baseline\n\n**Graph composition:**\n1. Creates nodes only for resources with planned changes\n2. Applies create-before-destroy ordering for replacements\n3. Establishes deposed object handling for replacements\n4. Sets up resource destruction sequences when needed\n\n#### EvalGraphBuilder\n\nUsed for validation and schema evaluation without configuring providers:\n\n- Retrieves provider schemas for type checking\n- Validates configuration structure\n- Does not initialize or configure actual provider instances\n\n### 1.4 Graph Transformers\n\nGraphTransformers modify graphs during construction. The interface is simple:\n\n```go\ntype GraphTransformer interface {\n    Transform(*Graph) error\n}\n```\n\nTransformers operate at different levels:\n\n**Key transformers in the pipeline:**\n\n1. **ConfigTransformer** - Adds resource nodes from configuration files\n2. **StateTransformer** - Adds state-only resources not in config\n3. **ProviderTransformer** - Adds provider nodes and connects them to resources\n4. **ReferenceTransformer** - Analyzes references and creates edges\n5. **ModuleExpansionTransformer** - Handles module.* expansion\n6. **CountTransformer** - Handles resource count expansion\n7. **ExpandTransformer** - Performs dynamic expansion with count/for_each\n8. **ProviderConfigTransformer** - Attaches configurations to providers\n9. **SchemaTransformer** - Attaches schema information to nodes\n10. **DeferredTransformer** - Marks operations for deferral when needed\n11. **OrphanResourceTransformer** - Handles removed resources\n12. **OutputTransformer** - Adds output value nodes\n13. **DestroyEdgeTransformer** - Creates edges for resource destruction\n14. **TransitiveReductionTransformer** - Removes redundant edges\n\n**Transformer execution order matters:** Transformers are applied sequentially, and later transformers depend on work done by earlier ones. For example, ReferenceTransformer must run after ConfigTransformer has added all resource nodes.\n\n### 1.5 Graph Representation\n\nThe Graph structure wraps a DAG (Directed Acyclic Graph):\n\n```go\ntype Graph struct {\n    dag.AcyclicGraph\n    Path addrs.ModuleInstance\n}\n```\n\nGraph nodes (vertices) represent different types of operations:\n- **Resource instances** - Individual resources being created/modified/deleted\n- **Providers** - Provider initialization and configuration\n- **Variables** - Root and module variable evaluation\n- **Outputs** - Output value evaluation\n- **Local values** - Local value computation\n- **Module instances** - Module expansion and nesting\n- **Data sources** - Data resource reads\n- **Checks** - Precondition and postcondition evaluation\n\nEdges represent dependencies:\n- **Reference edges** - A depends on B because B is referenced in A's configuration\n- **Implicit edges** - Dependencies within a module\n- **Provider edges** - Resources depend on their provider initialization\n- **Destroy edges** - Order constraints for destruction\n\n## 2. Provider Interface and Lifecycle\n\n### 2.1 Provider Architecture\n\nProviders are plugins implementing a well-defined interface. The architecture maintains a clean separation between Terraform core and provider implementations.\n\n**Provider lifecycle:**\n\n```\nInitialize → Configure → GetSchema → Read/Plan/Apply → Close\n```\n\n### 2.2 Provider Management\n\nThe `EvalContext` provides provider lifecycle management:\n\n```go\n// Initialization\nInitProvider(addr addrs.AbsProviderConfig, config *configs.Provider) (providers.Interface, error)\n\n// Access\nProvider(addr addrs.AbsProviderConfig) providers.Interface\nProviderSchema(addr addrs.AbsProviderConfig) (providers.ProviderSchema, error)\n\n// Configuration\nConfigureProvider(addr addrs.AbsProviderConfig, cfg cty.Value) tfdiags.Diagnostics\n\n// Cleanup\nCloseProvider(addr addrs.AbsProviderConfig) error\n```\n\n**Provider caching:**\n\nProviders are cached in the ContextGraphWalker to avoid repeated initialization:\n\n```go\ntype ContextGraphWalker struct {\n    providerCache map[string]providers.Interface      // Initialized providers\n    providerSchemas map[string]providers.ProviderSchema // Cached schemas\n    providerLock sync.Mutex                            // Thread-safe access\n}\n```\n\n### 2.3 Provider Node Execution\n\nProvider operations are represented as graph nodes:\n\n- **NodeApplyableProvider** - Initializes and configures a provider during apply\n- **NodeValidatableProvider** - Validates provider configuration during validation\n- **graphNodeCloseProvider** - Closes provider connections\n- **nodeExternalProvider** - Uses pre-configured providers passed from external callers\n\nWhen a provider node executes:\n1. It calls `EvalContext.InitProvider()` to create a provider instance\n2. It retrieves and validates the provider's schema\n3. It calls `ConfigureProvider()` with the provider configuration\n4. The provider instance is cached for use by resource operations\n\n### 2.4 Resource Operations\n\nResources delegate their operations to providers through standard interfaces:\n\n**Plan phase:**\n- Provider.PlanResourceChange() - Determines what changes are needed\n\n**Apply phase:**\n- Provider.ApplyResourceChange() - Applies the planned change\n- Provider.ImportResourceState() - Imports external resources\n\n**Refresh phase:**\n- Provider.ReadResource() - Gets current state from infrastructure\n\nEach resource operation node in the graph calls these provider methods within its Execute() method.\n\n### 2.5 Schema Management\n\nSchemas are retrieved once per provider and cached:\n\n```go\nschema, err := ctx.ProviderSchema(providerAddr)\n```\n\nSchemas define the resource types a provider supports and their configuration structure. They enable:\n- Type checking during expression evaluation\n- Validation of configuration values\n- Transformation of values during serialization\n\n## 3. State Management\n\n### 3.1 State Structure\n\nTerraform state represents the known infrastructure:\n\n```go\ntype State struct {\n    Version          uint64\n    Serial           uint64\n    Lineage          string\n    RootOutputValues map[string]*OutputValue\n    Modules          []*Module\n}\n```\n\nState tracks:\n- **Resources** - Resource instance values and metadata\n- **Outputs** - Root module output values\n- **Modules** - Nested module state\n- **Checks** - Check results and assertions\n\n### 3.2 Concurrent State Access: SyncState\n\nDuring graph traversal, multiple nodes execute concurrently. The `SyncState` wrapper provides thread-safe access:\n\n```go\ntype SyncState struct {\n    lock sync.Mutex\n    state *State\n}\n```\n\nSyncState consolidates multiple updates into atomic operations:\n\n```go\n// High-level atomic operations\nfunc (s *SyncState) SetResourceInstanceCurrent(addr addrs.AbsResourceInstance, obj *ResourceInstance, provider addrs.Provider)\nfunc (s *SyncState) SetResourceDeposed(addr addrs.AbsResourceInstance, key addrs.DeposedKey, obj *ResourceInstance, provider addrs.Provider)\nfunc (s *SyncState) RemoveResourceInstanceObject(addr addrs.AbsResourceInstance, key addrs.DeposedKey)\nfunc (s *SyncState) SetOutputValue(addr addrs.AbsOutputValue, value cty.Value)\n```\n\n**Key design:** Instead of locking individual fields, SyncState uses coarse-grained locking around meaningful state updates. This prevents partial updates and race conditions.\n\n### 3.3 State Snapshots\n\nThree state snapshots are maintained during pipeline execution:\n\n**InputState (PrevRunState):**\n- The state at the start of operations\n- Used to determine what already exists\n- Read-only during execution\n\n**CurrentState (State):**\n- Updated as resources are created/modified/deleted\n- Receives updates from Apply operations\n- Written to persistent storage at the end\n\n**RefreshState:**\n- Populated during refresh operations\n- Captures real infrastructure state\n- Used for comparison with configuration (plan operations)\n\n### 3.4 State Persistence\n\nState changes are persisted to backends through the Persister interface:\n\n```go\ntype Persister interface {\n    PersistState(*schemarepo.Schemas) error\n}\n```\n\n**Conflict detection:**\n- Serial numbers prevent overwriting concurrent changes\n- Lineage IDs track state history\n- Remote backends provide atomic writes\n\nAfter each apply phase, the updated state is persisted. The persistence layer handles:\n- Remote state locking\n- Concurrent write detection\n- State serialization\n- Backup creation\n\n### 3.5 Dynamic Expansion State\n\nThe `InstanceExpander` tracks gradual expansion of module and resource instances:\n\n```go\ntype Expander interface {\n    // Record that a module/resource at the given address expands to instances\n    SetModuleExpanded(addr addrs.ModuleInstance, for_each cty.Value)\n    SetResourceExpanded(addr addrs.AbsResourceInstance, for_each cty.Value)\n\n    // Get instances for a given address\n    GetModuleInstances(addr addrs.Module) []addrs.ModuleInstance\n    GetResourceInstances(addr addrs.Resource) []addrs.ResourceInstance\n}\n```\n\nThe expander allows count/for_each values to be unknown until they're evaluated during execution, enabling proper handling of dynamic resources.\n\n## 4. Execution Flow and Walker Pattern\n\n### 4.1 Graph Walking\n\nThe Graph.Walk() method traverses the graph and executes nodes:\n\n```go\nfunc (g *Graph) Walk(walker GraphWalker) tfdiags.Diagnostics {\n    // 1. Get evaluation context from walker\n    ctx := walker.EvalContext()\n\n    // 2. For each vertex in dependency order (respecting edges)\n    for vertex := range g.Vertices() {\n        // 3. Handle scope transitions (module entry/exit)\n        vertexCtx := walker.enterScope(vertex)\n\n        // 4. Execute the vertex if it's executable\n        if executable, ok := vertex.(GraphNodeExecutable); ok {\n            walker.Execute(vertexCtx, executable)\n        }\n\n        walker.exitScope(vertex)\n    }\n}\n```\n\n**Concurrency:** The graph walk uses the DAG's parallel traversal algorithm:\n- Only nodes with satisfied dependencies are executed\n- Multiple independent nodes execute concurrently\n- A semaphore limits parallelism (default 10)\n\n### 4.2 GraphWalker Interface\n\nThe GraphWalker coordinates execution:\n\n```go\ntype GraphWalker interface {\n    EvalContext() EvalContext\n    enterScope(evalContextScope) EvalContext\n    exitScope(evalContextScope)\n    Execute(EvalContext, GraphNodeExecutable) tfdiags.Diagnostics\n}\n```\n\n### 4.3 ContextGraphWalker Implementation\n\nThe main walker implementation provides the execution context:\n\n```go\ntype ContextGraphWalker struct {\n    // Configuration\n    Context *Context\n    Operation walkOperation\n\n    // State snapshots\n    State *states.SyncState           // Current state being updated\n    RefreshState *states.SyncState    // State from refresh\n    PrevRunState *states.SyncState    // Previous run's state\n\n    // Changes and tracking\n    Changes *plans.ChangesSync        // Planned changes\n    Checks *checks.State              // Check results\n    InstanceExpander *instances.Expander  // Dynamic expansion tracking\n    Deferrals *deferring.Deferred     // Deferred operations\n\n    // Caches\n    providerCache map[string]providers.Interface\n    provisionerCache map[string]provisioners.Interface\n    contexts collections.Map[evalContextScope, *BuiltinEvalContext]\n}\n```\n\n**Key operations:**\n\n1. **EvalContext()** - Creates the root evaluation context\n2. **enterScope()** - Creates module-specific contexts for nested modules\n3. **Execute()** - Calls the node's Execute method with a semaphore lock\n\n### 4.4 Node Execution\n\nEach executable node implements:\n\n```go\ntype GraphNodeExecutable interface {\n    Execute(ctx EvalContext, op walkOperation) tfdiags.Diagnostics\n}\n```\n\n**Example resource node execution:**\n\n```go\n// NodePlannableResourceInstance.Execute (plan phase)\nfunc (n *NodePlannableResourceInstance) Execute(ctx EvalContext, op walkOperation) tfdiags.Diagnostics {\n    // Get provider and schema\n    provider, schema := getProvider(ctx, n.ResolvedProvider)\n\n    // Read current state\n    prior := readState(ctx, n.Addr)\n\n    // Get proposed new state from config\n    proposed := evaluateConfig(ctx, n.Config)\n\n    // Call provider to plan changes\n    change := provider.PlanResourceChange(ctx, proposed, prior)\n\n    // Store the planned change\n    ctx.Changes().SetResourceInstancePlanned(n.Addr, change)\n}\n```\n\nDifferent node types execute different operations:\n- **Resource plan nodes** - Call provider.PlanResourceChange()\n- **Resource apply nodes** - Call provider.ApplyResourceChange()\n- **Provider nodes** - Call provider.Configure()\n- **Variable nodes** - Evaluate expressions\n- **Output nodes** - Evaluate output expressions\n- **Destroy nodes** - Handle resource deletion\n\n### 4.5 walkOperation Types\n\nThe walk operation indicates which phase is executing:\n\n```go\nconst (\n    walkPlan walkOperation = iota          // Plan phase\n    walkApply                              // Apply phase\n    walkValidate                           // Validation phase\n    walkImport                             // Import phase\n    walkRefresh                            // Refresh phase\n    walkPlanDestroy                        // Destroy plan phase\n    walkEval                               // Schema evaluation phase\n)\n```\n\nNodes can behave differently based on the operation. For example, resources skip refreshing during certain operations.\n\n### 4.6 Pipeline Coordination\n\nThe Context methods coordinate the overall pipeline:\n\n```go\n// Plan phase\nfunc (c *Context) Plan(config *configs.Config, prevRunState *states.State, opts *PlanOpts) (*plans.Plan, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n    // 1. Build the plan graph\n    graph, graphDiags := builder.Build(addrs.RootModule)\n\n    // 2. Create walker with input state\n    walker := c.graphWalker(graph, walkPlan, &graphWalkOpts{\n        InputState: prevRunState,\n        Changes: plans.NewChanges(),\n        Config: config,\n    })\n\n    // 3. Walk the graph\n    graph.Walk(walker)\n\n    // 4. Finalize the plan\n    plan := &plans.Plan{\n        Changes: walker.Changes.Finalize(),\n        State: walker.State.Close(),\n    }\n}\n\n// Apply phase\nfunc (c *Context) Apply(plan *plans.Plan, config *configs.Config, opts *ApplyOpts) (*states.State, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n    // 1. Build the apply graph (only for resources in plan)\n    graph, graphDiags := builder.Build(addrs.RootModule)\n\n    // 2. Create walker with changes from plan\n    walker := c.graphWalker(graph, walkApply, &graphWalkOpts{\n        InputState: plan.State,\n        Changes: plan.Changes,\n        Config: config,\n    })\n\n    // 3. Walk the graph\n    graph.Walk(walker)\n\n    // 4. Return final state\n    return walker.State.Close(), diags\n}\n```\n\n## 5. Hook System\n\n### 5.1 Hook Interface\n\nHooks provide extension points throughout the Terraform pipeline:\n\n```go\ntype Hook interface {\n    // Apply hooks\n    PreApply(id HookResourceIdentity, dk addrs.DeposedKey, action plans.Action, priorState, plannedNewState cty.Value) (HookAction, error)\n    PostApply(id HookResourceIdentity, dk addrs.DeposedKey, newState cty.Value, err error) (HookAction, error)\n\n    // Plan/diff hooks\n    PreDiff(id HookResourceIdentity, dk addrs.DeposedKey, priorState, proposedNewState cty.Value) (HookAction, error)\n    PostDiff(id HookResourceIdentity, dk addrs.DeposedKey, action plans.Action, priorState, plannedNewState cty.Value) (HookAction, error)\n\n    // Provisioning hooks\n    PreProvisionInstance(id HookResourceIdentity, state cty.Value) (HookAction, error)\n    PostProvisionInstance(id HookResourceIdentity, state cty.Value) (HookAction, error)\n    PreProvisionInstanceStep(id HookResourceIdentity, typeName string) (HookAction, error)\n    PostProvisionInstanceStep(id HookResourceIdentity, typeName string, err error) (HookAction, error)\n    ProvisionOutput(id HookResourceIdentity, typeName string, line string)\n\n    // Refresh hooks\n    PreRefresh(id HookResourceIdentity, dk addrs.DeposedKey, priorState cty.Value) (HookAction, error)\n    PostRefresh(id HookResourceIdentity, dk addrs.DeposedKey, priorState, newState cty.Value) (HookAction, error)\n\n    // Import hooks\n    PreImportState(id HookResourceIdentity, importID string) (HookAction, error)\n    PostImportState(id HookResourceIdentity, imported []providers.ImportedResource) (HookAction, error)\n    PrePlanImport(id HookResourceIdentity, importID string) (HookAction, error)\n    PostPlanImport(id HookResourceIdentity, imported []providers.ImportedResource) (HookAction, error)\n    PreApplyImport(id HookResourceIdentity, importing plans.ImportingSrc) (HookAction, error)\n    PostApplyImport(id HookResourceIdentity, importing plans.ImportingSrc) (HookAction, error)\n\n    // Lifecycle hooks\n    Stopping()                                              // Graceful shutdown signal\n    PostStateUpdate(new *states.State) (HookAction, error) // State changed\n}\n```\n\n### 5.2 Hook Invocation\n\nHooks are called through the EvalContext:\n\n```go\n// In BuiltinEvalContext\nfunc (ctx *BuiltinEvalContext) Hook(fn func(Hook) (HookAction, error)) error {\n    for _, h := range ctx.Hooks {\n        action, err := fn(h)\n        if err != nil {\n            return err\n        }\n        if action == HookActionHalt {\n            // Stop further hook processing\n            break\n        }\n    }\n    return nil\n}\n```\n\nHooks are registered when creating the Context:\n\n```go\nctx, diags := terraform.NewContext(&terraform.ContextOpts{\n    Hooks: []terraform.Hook{\n        uiHook,      // Updates UI with progress\n        countHook,   // Counts resources\n        stopHook,    // Handles graceful shutdown\n    },\n})\n```\n\n### 5.3 Hook Action Control\n\nHooks can influence execution through HookAction:\n\n```go\ntype HookAction byte\n\nconst (\n    HookActionContinue HookAction = iota  // Proceed normally\n    HookActionHalt                        // Stop this operation\n)\n```\n\nThis allows hooks to implement:\n- **Graceful shutdown** - Stop processing on external signals\n- **User approval** - Pause before critical operations\n- **Error injection** - Fail operations for testing\n- **Monitoring** - Pause and inspect operations\n\n## 6. Evaluation Context\n\n### 6.1 EvalContext Interface\n\nThe EvalContext provides the execution environment for graph nodes:\n\n```go\ntype EvalContext interface {\n    // Lifecycle\n    Stopped() <-chan struct{}\n\n    // Navigation\n    Path() addrs.ModuleInstance\n\n    // Hooks and UI\n    Hook(func(Hook) (HookAction, error)) error\n    Input() UIInput\n\n    // Providers\n    InitProvider(addr addrs.AbsProviderConfig, config *configs.Provider) (providers.Interface, error)\n    Provider(addr addrs.AbsProviderConfig) providers.Interface\n    ProviderSchema(addr addrs.AbsProviderConfig) (providers.ProviderSchema, error)\n    ConfigureProvider(addr addrs.AbsProviderConfig, cfg cty.Value) tfdiags.Diagnostics\n    CloseProvider(addr addrs.AbsProviderConfig) error\n\n    // Provisioners\n    Provisioner(name string) (provisioners.Interface, error)\n    ProvisionerSchema(name string) (*configschema.Block, error)\n    ClosePlugins() error\n\n    // State and changes\n    State() *states.SyncState\n    Changes() *plans.ChangesSync\n    RefreshState() *states.SyncState\n    PrevRunState() *states.SyncState\n\n    // Expression evaluation\n    EvaluateExpr(expr hcl.Expression, wantType cty.Type, self addrs.Referenceable) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics)\n    EvaluateBlock(block *configs.Block, self addrs.Referenceable, allowSelfRef bool) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics)\n\n    // Variable and value tracking\n    SetRootModuleArgument(addr addrs.InputVariable, value cty.Value)\n    GetLocalValue(addr addrs.LocalValue) cty.Value\n    SetLocalValue(addr addrs.LocalValue, value cty.Value)\n\n    // Dynamic expansion\n    InstanceExpander() *instances.Expander\n\n    // Deferred operations\n    Deferrals() *deferring.Deferred\n\n    // Check tracking\n    Checks() *checks.State\n\n    // Overrides\n    Overrides() *mocking.Overrides\n}\n```\n\n### 6.2 BuiltinEvalContext Implementation\n\nThe main evaluation context implementation:\n\n```go\ntype BuiltinEvalContext struct {\n    // Execution environment\n    StopContext context.Context\n    Hooks []Hook\n    InputValue UIInput\n\n    // Plugins and providers\n    Plugins *contextPlugins\n    ExternalProviderConfigs map[addrs.RootProviderConfig]providers.Interface\n    ProviderCache map[string]providers.Interface\n    ProviderSchemas map[string]providers.ProviderSchema\n    ProviderLock *sync.Mutex\n\n    // Provisioners\n    ProvisionerCache map[string]provisioners.Interface\n    ProvisionerSchemas map[string]*configschema.Block\n    ProvisionerLock *sync.Mutex\n\n    // State\n    StateValue *states.SyncState\n    RefreshStateValue *states.SyncState\n    PrevRunStateValue *states.SyncState\n\n    // Changes and tracking\n    ChangesValue *plans.ChangesSync\n    ChecksValue *checks.State\n    NamedValuesValue *namedvals.State\n    DeferralsValue *deferring.Deferred\n    InstanceExpanderValue *instances.Expander\n\n    // Evaluation\n    Evaluator *Evaluator\n}\n```\n\n### 6.3 Module-Scoped Contexts\n\nDifferent evaluation contexts are created for each module scope:\n\n```go\nfunc (w *ContextGraphWalker) enterScope(scope evalContextScope) EvalContext {\n    // Get or create a context for this module\n    if ctx, ok := w.contexts.GetOk(scope); ok {\n        return ctx\n    }\n\n    ctx := w.EvalContext().withScope(scope).(*BuiltinEvalContext)\n    w.contexts.Put(scope, ctx)\n    return ctx\n}\n```\n\nThis allows each module to have its own:\n- Variable values\n- Local values\n- Output values\n- Provider instances\n- Provisioner instances\n\n## 7. Dynamic Expansion for count/for_each\n\n### 7.1 Expansion Phases\n\nResources with count and for_each undergo multi-phase expansion:\n\n**Phase 1: Counting**\n```go\n// Evaluate count or for_each expression\nexpanded := evaluateCount(ctx, resource.Count)\n// Expand instances: aws_instance.web -> [aws_instance.web[0], aws_instance.web[1], ...]\nexpander.SetResourceExpanded(addr, expanded)\n```\n\n**Phase 2: Graph Update**\n```go\n// Dynamically add nodes for each expanded instance\nfor i, instance := range expanded {\n    g.Add(NewNodePlannableResourceInstance(...))\n}\n```\n\n**Phase 3: Execution**\n```go\n// Each instance node executes independently\nfor instance := range expanded {\n    walk the graph (may execute multiple instances concurrently)\n}\n```\n\n### 7.2 Deferred Expansion\n\nWhen count/for_each values are unknown during planning, resources are marked as deferred:\n\n```go\n// In node.Execute()\nif countValue.IsNull() || countValue.IsUnknown() {\n    // Record deferred action\n    deferrals.DeferResourceInstancePlanning(addr, deferralReason)\n    return // Skip this instance for now\n}\n```\n\nDeferred changes are applied in a subsequent run after dependencies provide the required values.\n\n## 8. Error Handling and Diagnostics\n\n### 8.1 Diagnostic Collection\n\nErrors and warnings are collected as diagnostics throughout execution:\n\n```go\ntype Diagnostics []Diagnostic\n\ntype Diagnostic interface {\n    Severity() DiagnosticSeverity  // Error, Warning\n    Description() DiagnosticDescription\n    Source() DiagnosticSource\n}\n```\n\nEach operation returns diagnostics:\n- **Plan returns** - Diagnostics if planning encountered issues\n- **Apply returns** - Diagnostics but still returns the updated state\n- **Nodes propagate** - Node.Execute() returns diagnostics\n\n### 8.2 Error Propagation\n\nGraph walking stops on errors:\n\n```go\n// In Graph.walk()\nfor vertex := range g.Vertices() {\n    diags = diags.Append(walker.Execute(vertexCtx, executable))\n    if diags.HasErrors() {\n        // Stop walking on errors\n        break\n    }\n}\n```\n\nNon-fatal errors can be collected and returned while continuing execution:\n\n```go\ntype NonFatalError struct {\n    Diagnostics Diagnostics\n}\n```\n\nThis allows partial results to be returned even when errors occur.\n\n### 8.3 Error Context\n\nErrors include source location information:\n\n```go\ntype DiagnosticSource struct {\n    Subject *SourceRange      // HCL source location\n    Context *SourceRange      // Surrounding context\n}\n```\n\nThis enables precise error reporting pointing to the exact configuration line that caused an issue.\n\n## 9. Extension Points in the Architecture\n\n### 9.1 Custom Graph Transformers\n\nExtend graph construction by implementing GraphTransformer:\n\n```go\ntype CustomTransformer struct {}\n\nfunc (t *CustomTransformer) Transform(g *Graph) error {\n    // Add custom nodes\n    g.Add(myCustomNode)\n\n    // Create edges\n    g.Connect(myCustomNode, someExistingNode)\n\n    return nil\n}\n```\n\nRegister in graph builders or apply to graphs after creation.\n\n### 9.2 Custom Hooks\n\nImplement Hook interface to observe and influence execution:\n\n```go\ntype CustomHook struct {}\n\nfunc (h *CustomHook) PreApply(id HookResourceIdentity, ...) (HookAction, error) {\n    // Log, monitor, or approve resource changes\n    log.Printf(\"About to apply %s\", id.Addr)\n    return HookActionContinue, nil\n}\n```\n\n### 9.3 Custom Evaluation Functions\n\nAdd custom evaluation capabilities:\n\n```go\n// In expression evaluation\nif customFunc := registry.GetFunction(name); customFunc != nil {\n    return customFunc.Call(args, ctx)\n}\n```\n\n### 9.4 Backend Integration\n\nExtend state management through backend interfaces:\n\n```go\ntype Backend interface {\n    // State management\n    State(workspace string) (statemgr.Full, error)\n\n    // Operation execution\n    Operation(context.Context, *operation.Operation) (*operation.Run, error)\n}\n```\n\nBackends can implement custom:\n- State locking mechanisms\n- Remote operations\n- State versioning\n- Access control\n\n## 10. Concurrent Execution Safety\n\n### 10.1 Concurrency Model\n\nThe architecture achieves thread-safe concurrent execution through:\n\n**1. Coarse-grained locking:**\n```go\n// SyncState locks entire operations\ntype SyncState struct {\n    lock sync.Mutex\n    state *State\n}\n\nfunc (s *SyncState) SetResourceInstanceCurrent(...) {\n    s.lock.Lock()\n    defer s.lock.Unlock()\n    s.state.SetResourceInstanceCurrent(...)\n}\n```\n\n**2. Semaphore-based parallelism:**\n```go\nfunc (w *ContextGraphWalker) Execute(ctx EvalContext, n GraphNodeExecutable) {\n    w.Context.parallelSem.Acquire()      // Limit concurrent execution\n    defer w.Context.parallelSem.Release()\n    n.Execute(ctx, w.Operation)\n}\n```\n\n**3. DAG-based ordering:**\n- Only nodes with satisfied dependencies execute\n- Dependencies prevent concurrent modification of same resources\n- Edge constraints ensure correct ordering\n\n### 10.2 State Synchronization\n\nMultiple independent state snapshots prevent conflicts:\n\n```go\n// During walk\nInputState (read-only) ← unchanged\nCurrentState ← updated by apply operations\nRefreshState ← updated by refresh operations\n```\n\nState snapshots enable:\n- Refreshing state without affecting current state\n- Comparing old vs new states\n- Atomic state transitions\n\n### 10.3 Provider Caching and Thread Safety\n\nProviders are cached and accessed safely:\n\n```go\ntype ContextGraphWalker struct {\n    providerCache map[string]providers.Interface\n    providerLock sync.Mutex\n}\n\nfunc (w *ContextGraphWalker) getProvider(name string) providers.Interface {\n    w.providerLock.Lock()\n    defer w.providerLock.Unlock()\n    return w.providerCache[name]\n}\n```\n\nEach provider instance is used by multiple resource nodes, but:\n- Individual provider calls are thread-safe (by provider contract)\n- Schema access is cached and read-only\n- Configuration is fixed before execution starts\n\n## 11. Summary of Data Flow\n\n### 11.1 Plan Phase Flow\n\n```\nUser Configuration (HCL)\n    ↓\nParse and validate configuration\n    ↓\nPlanGraphBuilder constructs graph:\n  - ConfigTransformer adds resource nodes\n  - ProviderTransformer adds provider nodes\n  - ReferenceTransformer creates dependency edges\n  - Other transformers complete graph\n    ↓\nContext.Plan() creates plan graph\n    ↓\nGraph.Walk() with walkPlan operation:\n  - Variable nodes evaluate input variables\n  - Provider nodes initialize and configure\n  - Resource nodes call provider.PlanResourceChange()\n  - Output nodes evaluate output expressions\n    ↓\nPlan captured with:\n  - Planned changes per resource\n  - Check results\n  - Evaluation state\n    ↓\nPlan returned to user/CLI\n```\n\n### 11.2 Apply Phase Flow\n\n```\nPlan (from previous phase or file)\n    ↓\nConfiguration (must match plan)\n    ↓\nApplyGraphBuilder constructs graph:\n  - Creates nodes only for resources in plan changes\n  - Handles create-before-destroy ordering\n  - Creates destruction edges for replaced resources\n    ↓\nContext.Apply() begins apply\n    ↓\nGraph.Walk() with walkApply operation:\n  - Provider nodes initialize and configure\n  - Resource nodes call provider.ApplyResourceChange()\n  - Changes update CurrentState synchronously\n  - PostApply hooks notify of completion\n  - Dependent resources can now execute\n    ↓\nState finalized:\n  - CurrentState becomes new persistent state\n  - Serial number incremented\n    ↓\nState persisted to backend:\n  - Remote locking acquired\n  - Atomic write performed\n  - Lock released\n    ↓\nUpdated state returned\n```\n\n### 11.3 Concurrent Execution Example\n\n```\nResource A\n  │\n  └─→ Provider A\n      └─→ (initializes once)\n\nResource B\n  │\n  └─→ Provider B\n      └─→ (initializes once)\n\nResource A depends on Resource B\n\nGraph execution:\n1. Provider A initializes (concurrent with Provider B)\n2. Provider B initializes (concurrent with Provider A)\n3. Resource B executes (uses Provider B)\n4. Resource A waits for Resource B dependency\n5. Resource A executes (uses Provider A)\n\nResult: A and B providers initialize concurrently,\n        B executes, then A executes sequentially.\n```\n\n## Conclusion\n\nTerraform's plan/apply pipeline architecture enables:\n- **Declarative infrastructure** through configuration-driven graphs\n- **Concurrent execution** of independent operations\n- **Safe state management** through synchronized updates\n- **Extensibility** through transformer and hook systems\n- **Reliable infrastructure changes** through planning and staged application\n\nThe graph-based model makes dependencies explicit, enables parallel execution where safe, and provides clear extension points for monitoring, control, and customization.\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":12,"cache_creation_input_tokens":2722,"cache_read_input_tokens":83470,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":2722},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"ccbdb57a-0f24-4452-a3f5-ad70759737cc","uuid":"87e91e01-b423-4951-bd39-53c7de8cba81"}

The architecture enables concurrent execution of independent operations while maintaining correct ordering of dependent operations.\n\nThe pipeline consists of three major phases:\n1. **Graph Construction** - Building a DAG of operations from configuration\n2. **Graph Traversal** - Executing graph nodes in dependency order\n3. **State Management** - Tracking and persisting infrastructure state\n\n## 1. Graph Builder System\n\n### 1.1 GraphBuilder Interface\n\nThe `GraphBuilder` interface is the foundational abstraction for constructing execution graphs:\n\n```go\ntype GraphBuilder interface {\n    Build(addrs.ModuleInstance) (*Graph, tfdiags.Diagnostics)\n}\n```\n\nGraph builders take configuration, state, and options as input and produce a complete execution graph ready for traversal.\n\n### 1.2 BasicGraphBuilder\n\nThe `BasicGraphBuilder` is the core implementation that applies a sequence of transformations:\n\n```go\ntype BasicGraphBuilder struct {\n    Steps []GraphTransformer\n    Name  string\n}\n\nfunc (b *BasicGraphBuilder) Build(path addrs.ModuleInstance) (*Graph, tfdiags.Diagnostics)\n```\n\nThe Build method:\n1. Creates an empty graph at the given module path\n2. Sequentially applies each GraphTransformer\n3. Validates the final graph structure\n4. Returns diagnostics for any errors during transformation\n\nEach transformer can add nodes, modify edges, or reorganize the graph structure. Transformers are applied in a specific order to ensure correct graph construction.\n\n### 1.3 Operation-Specific Graph Builders\n\n#### PlanGraphBuilder\n\nBuilds graphs for plan and plan-like operations (plan, plan-destroy, validate, import):\n\n**Key inputs:**\n- `Config` - The desired infrastructure configuration\n- `State` - The current state (for comparison)\n- `RootVariableValues` - Input variables for the root module\n- `ExternalProviderConfigs` - Pre-configured provider instances\n- `Targets` - Resource targeting for partial operations\n- `ForceReplace` - Resources to force replacement\n- `skipRefresh` - Whether to skip state refresh\n- `skipPlanChanges` - For refresh-only operations\n\n**Graph composition:**\n1. Creates resource nodes from configuration\n2. Attaches provider configurations and schemas\n3. Establishes dependencies based on references\n4. Handles count/for_each expansion\n5. Attaches validation and check nodes\n6. Applies targeting filters if specified\n\n#### ApplyGraphBuilder\n\nBuilds graphs for applying previously-generated plans:\n\n**Key inputs:**\n- `Config` - The configuration file (must match the plan's configuration)\n- `Changes` - The planned changes from the plan file\n- `State` - Current state used as a baseline\n\n**Graph composition:**\n1. Creates nodes only for resources with planned changes\n2. Applies create-before-destroy ordering for replacements\n3. Establishes deposed object handling for replacements\n4. Sets up resource destruction sequences when needed\n\n#### EvalGraphBuilder\n\nUsed for validation and schema evaluation without configuring providers:\n\n- Retrieves provider schemas for type checking\n- Validates configuration structure\n- Does not initialize or configure actual provider instances\n\n### 1.4 Graph Transformers\n\nGraphTransformers modify graphs during construction. The interface is simple:\n\n```go\ntype GraphTransformer interface {\n    Transform(*Graph) error\n}\n```\n\nTransformers operate at different levels:\n\n**Key transformers in the pipeline:**\n\n1. **ConfigTransformer** - Adds resource nodes from configuration files\n2. **StateTransformer** - Adds state-only resources not in config\n3. **ProviderTransformer** - Adds provider nodes and connects them to resources\n4. **ReferenceTransformer** - Analyzes references and creates edges\n5. **ModuleExpansionTransformer** - Handles module.* expansion\n6. **CountTransformer** - Handles resource count expansion\n7. **ExpandTransformer** - Performs dynamic expansion with count/for_each\n8. **ProviderConfigTransformer** - Attaches configurations to providers\n9. **SchemaTransformer** - Attaches schema information to nodes\n10. **DeferredTransformer** - Marks operations for deferral when needed\n11. **OrphanResourceTransformer** - Handles removed resources\n12. **OutputTransformer** - Adds output value nodes\n13. **DestroyEdgeTransformer** - Creates edges for resource destruction\n14. **TransitiveReductionTransformer** - Removes redundant edges\n\n**Transformer execution order matters:** Transformers are applied sequentially, and later transformers depend on work done by earlier ones. For example, ReferenceTransformer must run after ConfigTransformer has added all resource nodes.\n\n### 1.5 Graph Representation\n\nThe Graph structure wraps a DAG (Directed Acyclic Graph):\n\n```go\ntype Graph struct {\n    dag.AcyclicGraph\n    Path addrs.ModuleInstance\n}\n```\n\nGraph nodes (vertices) represent different types of operations:\n- **Resource instances** - Individual resources being created/modified/deleted\n- **Providers** - Provider initialization and configuration\n- **Variables** - Root and module variable evaluation\n- **Outputs** - Output value evaluation\n- **Local values** - Local value computation\n- **Module instances** - Module expansion and nesting\n- **Data sources** - Data resource reads\n- **Checks** - Precondition and postcondition evaluation\n\nEdges represent dependencies:\n- **Reference edges** - A depends on B because B is referenced in A's configuration\n- **Implicit edges** - Dependencies within a module\n- **Provider edges** - Resources depend on their provider initialization\n- **Destroy edges** - Order constraints for destruction\n\n## 2. Provider Interface and Lifecycle\n\n### 2.1 Provider Architecture\n\nProviders are plugins implementing a well-defined interface. The architecture maintains a clean separation between Terraform core and provider implementations.\n\n**Provider lifecycle:**\n\n```\nInitialize → Configure → GetSchema → Read/Plan/Apply → Close\n```\n\n### 2.2 Provider Management\n\nThe `EvalContext` provides provider lifecycle management:\n\n```go\n// Initialization\nInitProvider(addr addrs.AbsProviderConfig, config *configs.Provider) (providers.Interface, error)\n\n// Access\nProvider(addr addrs.AbsProviderConfig) providers.Interface\nProviderSchema(addr addrs.AbsProviderConfig) (providers.ProviderSchema, error)\n\n// Configuration\nConfigureProvider(addr addrs.AbsProviderConfig, cfg cty.Value) tfdiags.Diagnostics\n\n// Cleanup\nCloseProvider(addr addrs.AbsProviderConfig) error\n```\n\n**Provider caching:**\n\nProviders are cached in the ContextGraphWalker to avoid repeated initialization:\n\n```go\ntype ContextGraphWalker struct {\n    providerCache map[string]providers.Interface      // Initialized providers\n    providerSchemas map[string]providers.ProviderSchema // Cached schemas\n    providerLock sync.Mutex                            // Thread-safe access\n}\n```\n\n### 2.3 Provider Node Execution\n\nProvider operations are represented as graph nodes:\n\n- **NodeApplyableProvider** - Initializes and configures a provider during apply\n- **NodeValidatableProvider** - Validates provider configuration during validation\n- **graphNodeCloseProvider** - Closes provider connections\n- **nodeExternalProvider** - Uses pre-configured providers passed from external callers\n\nWhen a provider node executes:\n1. It calls `EvalContext.InitProvider()` to create a provider instance\n2. It retrieves and validates the provider's schema\n3. It calls `ConfigureProvider()` with the provider configuration\n4. The provider instance is cached for use by resource operations\n\n### 2.4 Resource Operations\n\nResources delegate their operations to providers through standard interfaces:\n\n**Plan phase:**\n- Provider.PlanResourceChange() - Determines what changes are needed\n\n**Apply phase:**\n- Provider.ApplyResourceChange() - Applies the planned change\n- Provider.ImportResourceState() - Imports external resources\n\n**Refresh phase:**\n- Provider.ReadResource() - Gets current state from infrastructure\n\nEach resource operation node in the graph calls these provider methods within its Execute() method.\n\n### 2.5 Schema Management\n\nSchemas are retrieved once per provider and cached:\n\n```go\nschema, err := ctx.ProviderSchema(providerAddr)\n```\n\nSchemas define the resource types a provider supports and their configuration structure. They enable:\n- Type checking during expression evaluation\n- Validation of configuration values\n- Transformation of values during serialization\n\n## 3. State Management\n\n### 3.1 State Structure\n\nTerraform state represents the known infrastructure:\n\n```go\ntype State struct {\n    Version          uint64\n    Serial           uint64\n    Lineage          string\n    RootOutputValues map[string]*OutputValue\n    Modules          []*Module\n}\n```\n\nState tracks:\n- **Resources** - Resource instance values and metadata\n- **Outputs** - Root module output values\n- **Modules** - Nested module state\n- **Checks** - Check results and assertions\n\n### 3.2 Concurrent State Access: SyncState\n\nDuring graph traversal, multiple nodes execute concurrently. The `SyncState` wrapper provides thread-safe access:\n\n```go\ntype SyncState struct {\n    lock sync.Mutex\n    state *State\n}\n```\n\nSyncState consolidates multiple updates into atomic operations:\n\n```go\n// High-level atomic operations\nfunc (s *SyncState) SetResourceInstanceCurrent(addr addrs.AbsResourceInstance, obj *ResourceInstance, provider addrs.Provider)\nfunc (s *SyncState) SetResourceDeposed(addr addrs.AbsResourceInstance, key addrs.DeposedKey, obj *ResourceInstance, provider addrs.Provider)\nfunc (s *SyncState) RemoveResourceInstanceObject(addr addrs.AbsResourceInstance, key addrs.DeposedKey)\nfunc (s *SyncState) SetOutputValue(addr addrs.AbsOutputValue, value cty.Value)\n```\n\n**Key design:** Instead of locking individual fields, SyncState uses coarse-grained locking around meaningful state updates. This prevents partial updates and race conditions.\n\n### 3.3 State Snapshots\n\nThree state snapshots are maintained during pipeline execution:\n\n**InputState (PrevRunState):**\n- The state at the start of operations\n- Used to determine what already exists\n- Read-only during execution\n\n**CurrentState (State):**\n- Updated as resources are created/modified/deleted\n- Receives updates from Apply operations\n- Written to persistent storage at the end\n\n**RefreshState:**\n- Populated during refresh operations\n- Captures real infrastructure state\n- Used for comparison with configuration (plan operations)\n\n### 3.4 State Persistence\n\nState changes are persisted to backends through the Persister interface:\n\n```go\ntype Persister interface {\n    PersistState(*schemarepo.Schemas) error\n}\n```\n\n**Conflict detection:**\n- Serial numbers prevent overwriting concurrent changes\n- Lineage IDs track state history\n- Remote backends provide atomic writes\n\nAfter each apply phase, the updated state is persisted. The persistence layer handles:\n- Remote state locking\n- Concurrent write detection\n- State serialization\n- Backup creation\n\n### 3.5 Dynamic Expansion State\n\nThe `InstanceExpander` tracks gradual expansion of module and resource instances:\n\n```go\ntype Expander interface {\n    // Record that a module/resource at the given address expands to instances\n    SetModuleExpanded(addr addrs.ModuleInstance, for_each cty.Value)\n    SetResourceExpanded(addr addrs.AbsResourceInstance, for_each cty.Value)\n\n    // Get instances for a given address\n    GetModuleInstances(addr addrs.Module) []addrs.ModuleInstance\n    GetResourceInstances(addr addrs.Resource) []addrs.ResourceInstance\n}\n```\n\nThe expander allows count/for_each values to be unknown until they're evaluated during execution, enabling proper handling of dynamic resources.\n\n## 4. Execution Flow and Walker Pattern\n\n### 4.1 Graph Walking\n\nThe Graph.Walk() method traverses the graph and executes nodes:\n\n```go\nfunc (g *Graph) Walk(walker GraphWalker) tfdiags.Diagnostics {\n    // 1. Get evaluation context from walker\n    ctx := walker.EvalContext()\n\n    // 2. For each vertex in dependency order (respecting edges)\n    for vertex := range g.Vertices() {\n        // 3. Handle scope transitions (module entry/exit)\n        vertexCtx := walker.enterScope(vertex)\n\n        // 4. Execute the vertex if it's executable\n        if executable, ok := vertex.(GraphNodeExecutable); ok {\n            walker.Execute(vertexCtx, executable)\n        }\n\n        walker.exitScope(vertex)\n    }\n}\n```\n\n**Concurrency:** The graph walk uses the DAG's parallel traversal algorithm:\n- Only nodes with satisfied dependencies are executed\n- Multiple independent nodes execute concurrently\n- A semaphore limits parallelism (default 10)\n\n### 4.2 GraphWalker Interface\n\nThe GraphWalker coordinates execution:\n\n```go\ntype GraphWalker interface {\n    EvalContext() EvalContext\n    enterScope(evalContextScope) EvalContext\n    exitScope(evalContextScope)\n    Execute(EvalContext, GraphNodeExecutable) tfdiags.Diagnostics\n}\n```\n\n### 4.3 ContextGraphWalker Implementation\n\nThe main walker implementation provides the execution context:\n\n```go\ntype ContextGraphWalker struct {\n    // Configuration\n    Context *Context\n    Operation walkOperation\n\n    // State snapshots\n    State *states.SyncState           // Current state being updated\n    RefreshState *states.SyncState    // State from refresh\n    PrevRunState *states.SyncState    // Previous run's state\n\n    // Changes and tracking\n    Changes *plans.ChangesSync        // Planned changes\n    Checks *checks.State              // Check results\n    InstanceExpander *instances.Expander  // Dynamic expansion tracking\n    Deferrals *deferring.Deferred     // Deferred operations\n\n    // Caches\n    providerCache map[string]providers.Interface\n    provisionerCache map[string]provisioners.Interface\n    contexts collections.Map[evalContextScope, *BuiltinEvalContext]\n}\n```\n\n**Key operations:**\n\n1. **EvalContext()** - Creates the root evaluation context\n2. **enterScope()** - Creates module-specific contexts for nested modules\n3. **Execute()** - Calls the node's Execute method with a semaphore lock\n\n### 4.4 Node Execution\n\nEach executable node implements:\n\n```go\ntype GraphNodeExecutable interface {\n    Execute(ctx EvalContext, op walkOperation) tfdiags.Diagnostics\n}\n```\n\n**Example resource node execution:**\n\n```go\n// NodePlannableResourceInstance.Execute (plan phase)\nfunc (n *NodePlannableResourceInstance) Execute(ctx EvalContext, op walkOperation) tfdiags.Diagnostics {\n    // Get provider and schema\n    provider, schema := getProvider(ctx, n.ResolvedProvider)\n\n    // Read current state\n    prior := readState(ctx, n.Addr)\n\n    // Get proposed new state from config\n    proposed := evaluateConfig(ctx, n.Config)\n\n    // Call provider to plan changes\n    change := provider.PlanResourceChange(ctx, proposed, prior)\n\n    // Store the planned change\n    ctx.Changes().SetResourceInstancePlanned(n.Addr, change)\n}\n```\n\nDifferent node types execute different operations:\n- **Resource plan nodes** - Call provider.PlanResourceChange()\n- **Resource apply nodes** - Call provider.ApplyResourceChange()\n- **Provider nodes** - Call provider.Configure()\n- **Variable nodes** - Evaluate expressions\n- **Output nodes** - Evaluate output expressions\n- **Destroy nodes** - Handle resource deletion\n\n### 4.5 walkOperation Types\n\nThe walk operation indicates which phase is executing:\n\n```go\nconst (\n    walkPlan walkOperation = iota          // Plan phase\n    walkApply                              // Apply phase\n    walkValidate                           // Validation phase\n    walkImport                             // Import phase\n    walkRefresh                            // Refresh phase\n    walkPlanDestroy                        // Destroy plan phase\n    walkEval                               // Schema evaluation phase\n)\n```\n\nNodes can behave differently based on the operation. For example, resources skip refreshing during certain operations.\n\n### 4.6 Pipeline Coordination\n\nThe Context methods coordinate the overall pipeline:\n\n```go\n// Plan phase\nfunc (c *Context) Plan(config *configs.Config, prevRunState *states.State, opts *PlanOpts) (*plans.Plan, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n    // 1. Build the plan graph\n    graph, graphDiags := builder.Build(addrs.RootModule)\n\n    // 2. Create walker with input state\n    walker := c.graphWalker(graph, walkPlan, &graphWalkOpts{\n        InputState: prevRunState,\n        Changes: plans.NewChanges(),\n        Config: config,\n    })\n\n    // 3. Walk the graph\n    graph.Walk(walker)\n\n    // 4. Finalize the plan\n    plan := &plans.Plan{\n        Changes: walker.Changes.Finalize(),\n        State: walker.State.Close(),\n    }\n}\n\n// Apply phase\nfunc (c *Context) Apply(plan *plans.Plan, config *configs.Config, opts *ApplyOpts) (*states.State, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n    // 1. Build the apply graph (only for resources in plan)\n    graph, graphDiags := builder.Build(addrs.RootModule)\n\n    // 2. Create walker with changes from plan\n    walker := c.graphWalker(graph, walkApply, &graphWalkOpts{\n        InputState: plan.State,\n        Changes: plan.Changes,\n        Config: config,\n    })\n\n    // 3. Walk the graph\n    graph.Walk(walker)\n\n    // 4. Return final state\n    return walker.State.Close(), diags\n}\n```\n\n## 5. Hook System\n\n### 5.1 Hook Interface\n\nHooks provide extension points throughout the Terraform pipeline:\n\n```go\ntype Hook interface {\n    // Apply hooks\n    PreApply(id HookResourceIdentity, dk addrs.DeposedKey, action plans.Action, priorState, plannedNewState cty.Value) (HookAction, error)\n    PostApply(id HookResourceIdentity, dk addrs.DeposedKey, newState cty.Value, err error) (HookAction, error)\n\n    // Plan/diff hooks\n    PreDiff(id HookResourceIdentity, dk addrs.DeposedKey, priorState, proposedNewState cty.Value) (HookAction, error)\n    PostDiff(id HookResourceIdentity, dk addrs.DeposedKey, action plans.Action, priorState, plannedNewState cty.Value) (HookAction, error)\n\n    // Provisioning hooks\n    PreProvisionInstance(id HookResourceIdentity, state cty.Value) (HookAction, error)\n    PostProvisionInstance(id HookResourceIdentity, state cty.Value) (HookAction, error)\n    PreProvisionInstanceStep(id HookResourceIdentity, typeName string) (HookAction, error)\n    PostProvisionInstanceStep(id HookResourceIdentity, typeName string, err error) (HookAction, error)\n    ProvisionOutput(id HookResourceIdentity, typeName string, line string)\n\n    // Refresh hooks\n    PreRefresh(id HookResourceIdentity, dk addrs.DeposedKey, priorState cty.Value) (HookAction, error)\n    PostRefresh(id HookResourceIdentity, dk addrs.DeposedKey, priorState, newState cty.Value) (HookAction, error)\n\n    // Import hooks\n    PreImportState(id HookResourceIdentity, importID string) (HookAction, error)\n    PostImportState(id HookResourceIdentity, imported []providers.ImportedResource) (HookAction, error)\n    PrePlanImport(id HookResourceIdentity, importID string) (HookAction, error)\n    PostPlanImport(id HookResourceIdentity, imported []providers.ImportedResource) (HookAction, error)\n    PreApplyImport(id HookResourceIdentity, importing plans.ImportingSrc) (HookAction, error)\n    PostApplyImport(id HookResourceIdentity, importing plans.ImportingSrc) (HookAction, error)\n\n    // Lifecycle hooks\n    Stopping()                                              // Graceful shutdown signal\n    PostStateUpdate(new *states.State) (HookAction, error) // State changed\n}\n```\n\n### 5.2 Hook Invocation\n\nHooks are called through the EvalContext:\n\n```go\n// In BuiltinEvalContext\nfunc (ctx *BuiltinEvalContext) Hook(fn func(Hook) (HookAction, error)) error {\n    for _, h := range ctx.Hooks {\n        action, err := fn(h)\n        if err != nil {\n            return err\n        }\n        if action == HookActionHalt {\n            // Stop further hook processing\n            break\n        }\n    }\n    return nil\n}\n```\n\nHooks are registered when creating the Context:\n\n```go\nctx, diags := terraform.NewContext(&terraform.ContextOpts{\n    Hooks: []terraform.Hook{\n        uiHook,      // Updates UI with progress\n        countHook,   // Counts resources\n        stopHook,    // Handles graceful shutdown\n    },\n})\n```\n\n### 5.3 Hook Action Control\n\nHooks can influence execution through HookAction:\n\n```go\ntype HookAction byte\n\nconst (\n    HookActionContinue HookAction = iota  // Proceed normally\n    HookActionHalt                        // Stop this operation\n)\n```\n\nThis allows hooks to implement:\n- **Graceful shutdown** - Stop processing on external signals\n- **User approval** - Pause before critical operations\n- **Error injection** - Fail operations for testing\n- **Monitoring** - Pause and inspect operations\n\n## 6. Evaluation Context\n\n### 6.1 EvalContext Interface\n\nThe EvalContext provides the execution environment for graph nodes:\n\n```go\ntype EvalContext interface {\n    // Lifecycle\n    Stopped() <-chan struct{}\n\n    // Navigation\n    Path() addrs.ModuleInstance\n\n    // Hooks and UI\n    Hook(func(Hook) (HookAction, error)) error\n    Input() UIInput\n\n    // Providers\n    InitProvider(addr addrs.AbsProviderConfig, config *configs.Provider) (providers.Interface, error)\n    Provider(addr addrs.AbsProviderConfig) providers.Interface\n    ProviderSchema(addr addrs.AbsProviderConfig) (providers.ProviderSchema, error)\n    ConfigureProvider(addr addrs.AbsProviderConfig, cfg cty.Value) tfdiags.Diagnostics\n    CloseProvider(addr addrs.AbsProviderConfig) error\n\n    // Provisioners\n    Provisioner(name string) (provisioners.Interface, error)\n    ProvisionerSchema(name string) (*configschema.Block, error)\n    ClosePlugins() error\n\n    // State and changes\n    State() *states.SyncState\n    Changes() *plans.ChangesSync\n    RefreshState() *states.SyncState\n    PrevRunState() *states.SyncState\n\n    // Expression evaluation\n    EvaluateExpr(expr hcl.Expression, wantType cty.Type, self addrs.Referenceable) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics)\n    EvaluateBlock(block *configs.Block, self addrs.Referenceable, allowSelfRef bool) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics)\n\n    // Variable and value tracking\n    SetRootModuleArgument(addr addrs.InputVariable, value cty.Value)\n    GetLocalValue(addr addrs.LocalValue) cty.Value\n    SetLocalValue(addr addrs.LocalValue, value cty.Value)\n\n    // Dynamic expansion\n    InstanceExpander() *instances.Expander\n\n    // Deferred operations\n    Deferrals() *deferring.Deferred\n\n    // Check tracking\n    Checks() *checks.State\n\n    // Overrides\n    Overrides() *mocking.Overrides\n}\n```\n\n### 6.2 BuiltinEvalContext Implementation\n\nThe main evaluation context implementation:\n\n```go\ntype BuiltinEvalContext struct {\n    // Execution environment\n    StopContext context.Context\n    Hooks []Hook\n    InputValue UIInput\n\n    // Plugins and providers\n    Plugins *contextPlugins\n    ExternalProviderConfigs map[addrs.RootProviderConfig]providers.Interface\n    ProviderCache map[string]providers.Interface\n    ProviderSchemas map[string]providers.ProviderSchema\n    ProviderLock *sync.Mutex\n\n    // Provisioners\n    ProvisionerCache map[string]provisioners.Interface\n    ProvisionerSchemas map[string]*configschema.Block\n    ProvisionerLock *sync.Mutex\n\n    // State\n    StateValue *states.SyncState\n    RefreshStateValue *states.SyncState\n    PrevRunStateValue *states.SyncState\n\n    // Changes and tracking\n    ChangesValue *plans.ChangesSync\n    ChecksValue *checks.State\n    NamedValuesValue *namedvals.State\n    DeferralsValue *deferring.Deferred\n    InstanceExpanderValue *instances.Expander\n\n    // Evaluation\n    Evaluator *Evaluator\n}\n```\n\n### 6.3 Module-Scoped Contexts\n\nDifferent evaluation contexts are created for each module scope:\n\n```go\nfunc (w *ContextGraphWalker) enterScope(scope evalContextScope) EvalContext {\n    // Get or create a context for this module\n    if ctx, ok := w.contexts.GetOk(scope); ok {\n        return ctx\n    }\n\n    ctx := w.EvalContext().withScope(scope).(*BuiltinEvalContext)\n    w.contexts.Put(scope, ctx)\n    return ctx\n}\n```\n\nThis allows each module to have its own:\n- Variable values\n- Local values\n- Output values\n- Provider instances\n- Provisioner instances\n\n## 7. Dynamic Expansion for count/for_each\n\n### 7.1 Expansion Phases\n\nResources with count and for_each undergo multi-phase expansion:\n\n**Phase 1: Counting**\n```go\n// Evaluate count or for_each expression\nexpanded := evaluateCount(ctx, resource.Count)\n// Expand instances: aws_instance.web -> [aws_instance.web[0], aws_instance.web[1], ...]\nexpander.SetResourceExpanded(addr, expanded)\n```\n\n**Phase 2: Graph Update**\n```go\n// Dynamically add nodes for each expanded instance\nfor i, instance := range expanded {\n    g.Add(NewNodePlannableResourceInstance(...))\n}\n```\n\n**Phase 3: Execution**\n```go\n// Each instance node executes independently\nfor instance := range expanded {\n    walk the graph (may execute multiple instances concurrently)\n}\n```\n\n### 7.2 Deferred Expansion\n\nWhen count/for_each values are unknown during planning, resources are marked as deferred:\n\n```go\n// In node.Execute()\nif countValue.IsNull() || countValue.IsUnknown() {\n    // Record deferred action\n    deferrals.DeferResourceInstancePlanning(addr, deferralReason)\n    return // Skip this instance for now\n}\n```\n\nDeferred changes are applied in a subsequent run after dependencies provide the required values.\n\n## 8. Error Handling and Diagnostics\n\n### 8.1 Diagnostic Collection\n\nErrors and warnings are collected as diagnostics throughout execution:\n\n```go\ntype Diagnostics []Diagnostic\n\ntype Diagnostic interface {\n    Severity() DiagnosticSeverity  // Error, Warning\n    Description() DiagnosticDescription\n    Source() DiagnosticSource\n}\n```\n\nEach operation returns diagnostics:\n- **Plan returns** - Diagnostics if planning encountered issues\n- **Apply returns** - Diagnostics but still returns the updated state\n- **Nodes propagate** - Node.Execute() returns diagnostics\n\n### 8.2 Error Propagation\n\nGraph walking stops on errors:\n\n```go\n// In Graph.walk()\nfor vertex := range g.Vertices() {\n    diags = diags.Append(walker.Execute(vertexCtx, executable))\n    if diags.HasErrors() {\n        // Stop walking on errors\n        break\n    }\n}\n```\n\nNon-fatal errors can be collected and returned while continuing execution:\n\n```go\ntype NonFatalError struct {\n    Diagnostics Diagnostics\n}\n```\n\nThis allows partial results to be returned even when errors occur.\n\n### 8.3 Error Context\n\nErrors include source location information:\n\n```go\ntype DiagnosticSource struct {\n    Subject *SourceRange      // HCL source location\n    Context *SourceRange      // Surrounding context\n}\n```\n\nThis enables precise error reporting pointing to the exact configuration line that caused an issue.\n\n## 9. Extension Points in the Architecture\n\n### 9.1 Custom Graph Transformers\n\nExtend graph construction by implementing GraphTransformer:\n\n```go\ntype CustomTransformer struct {}\n\nfunc (t *CustomTransformer) Transform(g *Graph) error {\n    // Add custom nodes\n    g.Add(myCustomNode)\n\n    // Create edges\n    g.Connect(myCustomNode, someExistingNode)\n\n    return nil\n}\n```\n\nRegister in graph builders or apply to graphs after creation.\n\n### 9.2 Custom Hooks\n\nImplement Hook interface to observe and influence execution:\n\n```go\ntype CustomHook struct {}\n\nfunc (h *CustomHook) PreApply(id HookResourceIdentity, ...) (HookAction, error) {\n    // Log, monitor, or approve resource changes\n    log.Printf(\"About to apply %s\", id.Addr)\n    return HookActionContinue, nil\n}\n```\n\n### 9.3 Custom Evaluation Functions\n\nAdd custom evaluation capabilities:\n\n```go\n// In expression evaluation\nif customFunc := registry.GetFunction(name); customFunc != nil {\n    return customFunc.Call(args, ctx)\n}\n```\n\n### 9.4 Backend Integration\n\nExtend state management through backend interfaces:\n\n```go\ntype Backend interface {\n    // State management\n    State(workspace string) (statemgr.Full, error)\n\n    // Operation execution\n    Operation(context.Context, *operation.Operation) (*operation.Run, error)\n}\n```\n\nBackends can implement custom:\n- State locking mechanisms\n- Remote operations\n- State versioning\n- Access control\n\n## 10. Concurrent Execution Safety\n\n### 10.1 Concurrency Model\n\nThe architecture achieves thread-safe concurrent execution through:\n\n**1. Coarse-grained locking:**\n```go\n// SyncState locks entire operations\ntype SyncState struct {\n    lock sync.Mutex\n    state *State\n}\n\nfunc (s *SyncState) SetResourceInstanceCurrent(...) {\n    s.lock.Lock()\n    defer s.lock.Unlock()\n    s.state.SetResourceInstanceCurrent(...)\n}\n```\n\n**2. Semaphore-based parallelism:**\n```go\nfunc (w *ContextGraphWalker) Execute(ctx EvalContext, n GraphNodeExecutable) {\n    w.Context.parallelSem.Acquire()      // Limit concurrent execution\n    defer w.Context.parallelSem.Release()\n    n.Execute(ctx, w.Operation)\n}\n```\n\n**3. DAG-based ordering:**\n- Only nodes with satisfied dependencies execute\n- Dependencies prevent concurrent modification of same resources\n- Edge constraints ensure correct ordering\n\n### 10.2 State Synchronization\n\nMultiple independent state snapshots prevent conflicts:\n\n```go\n// During walk\nInputState (read-only) ← unchanged\nCurrentState ← updated by apply operations\nRefreshState ← updated by refresh operations\n```\n\nState snapshots enable:\n- Refreshing state without affecting current state\n- Comparing old vs new states\n- Atomic state transitions\n\n### 10.3 Provider Caching and Thread Safety\n\nProviders are cached and accessed safely:\n\n```go\ntype ContextGraphWalker struct {\n    providerCache map[string]providers.Interface\n    providerLock sync.Mutex\n}\n\nfunc (w *ContextGraphWalker) getProvider(name string) providers.Interface {\n    w.providerLock.Lock()\n    defer w.providerLock.Unlock()\n    return w.providerCache[name]\n}\n```\n\nEach provider instance is used by multiple resource nodes, but:\n- Individual provider calls are thread-safe (by provider contract)\n- Schema access is cached and read-only\n- Configuration is fixed before execution starts\n\n## 11. Summary of Data Flow\n\n### 11.1 Plan Phase Flow\n\n```\nUser Configuration (HCL)\n    ↓\nParse and validate configuration\n    ↓\nPlanGraphBuilder constructs graph:\n  - ConfigTransformer adds resource nodes\n  - ProviderTransformer adds provider nodes\n  - ReferenceTransformer creates dependency edges\n  - Other transformers complete graph\n    ↓\nContext.Plan() creates plan graph\n    ↓\nGraph.Walk() with walkPlan operation:\n  - Variable nodes evaluate input variables\n  - Provider nodes initialize and configure\n  - Resource nodes call provider.PlanResourceChange()\n  - Output nodes evaluate output expressions\n    ↓\nPlan captured with:\n  - Planned changes per resource\n  - Check results\n  - Evaluation state\n    ↓\nPlan returned to user/CLI\n```\n\n### 11.2 Apply Phase Flow\n\n```\nPlan (from previous phase or file)\n    ↓\nConfiguration (must match plan)\n    ↓\nApplyGraphBuilder constructs graph:\n  - Creates nodes only for resources in plan changes\n  - Handles create-before-destroy ordering\n  - Creates destruction edges for replaced resources\n    ↓\nContext.Apply() begins apply\n    ↓\nGraph.Walk() with walkApply operation:\n  - Provider nodes initialize and configure\n  - Resource nodes call provider.ApplyResourceChange()\n  - Changes update CurrentState synchronously\n  - PostApply hooks notify of completion\n  - Dependent resources can now execute\n    ↓\nState finalized:\n  - CurrentState becomes new persistent state\n  - Serial number incremented\n    ↓\nState persisted to backend:\n  - Remote locking acquired\n  - Atomic write performed\n  - Lock released\n    ↓\nUpdated state returned\n```\n\n### 11.3 Concurrent Execution Example\n\n```\nResource A\n  │\n  └─→ Provider A\n      └─→ (initializes once)\n\nResource B\n  │\n  └─→ Provider B\n      └─→ (initializes once)\n\nResource A depends on Resource B\n\nGraph execution:\n1. Provider A initializes (concurrent with Provider B)\n2. Provider B initializes (concurrent with Provider A)\n3. Resource B executes (uses Provider B)\n4. Resource A waits for Resource B dependency\n5. Resource A executes (uses Provider A)\n\nResult: A and B providers initialize concurrently,\n        B executes, then A executes sequentially.\n```\n\n## Conclusion\n\nTerraform's plan/apply pipeline architecture enables:\n- **Declarative infrastructure** through configuration-driven graphs\n- **Concurrent execution** of independent operations\n- **Safe state management** through synchronized updates\n- **Extensibility** through transformer and hook systems\n- **Reliable infrastructure changes** through planning and staged application\n\nThe graph-based model makes dependencies explicit, enables parallel execution where safe, and provides clear extension points for monitoring, control, and customization.\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
